Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it «cure for contusion», and that is what you do behind the patient who has this disease the hairs which he has on the forehead, then make III cuts on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II fingers exactly in the middle of the forehead downwards towards the nose, and the other two at the sides above the temples, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at the sides above the temples; and move your hand away from the connection of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then pour the spatumile agut from both sides where this form is.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut which is near the temple to the second cut; and peel off all the skin that is between the two cuts on the entire surface that is over the bone, then do the same from the middle cut to the other second one, and then extract this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so place in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side towards the flesh near the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous up to where it opens near the heart, and then do the same in the middle cut until the other end; and then draw blood evenly, and press the area for blood release; then place in each cut a wick of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened with wine and oil and elderflower, and be careful that hot abscesses do not occur; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the realm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to anyone comes acute catarrh usually, and you see the eyes dim and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and in the head there comes sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from any other source than many veins, and the best cure that there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie back with his head up, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on the wide temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, then wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen threads; then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances, which promote fleshing over.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flower, and of colofonium four parts, and make a plaster; and administer it on these wounds to quicken the flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or insects, or small stones or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas, lentils; or flowing substances such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or flaxseed oil, then perform extraction; and make him sneeze with condysium, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often pus comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then perform extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then perform extraction with a fine needle of small doublet; and if it does not come out by this means, make a tube of brass and place the end of the tube in the opening of the ear tightly, and plug what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out forcefully, as often pus comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glue from which birds are caught, and place some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not leap free from all these things that we have said, then you must quickly cut the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come; and the method of the cutting is such that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and cut a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat where it depends; and let the cut be like a crescent until you come to the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily with your mouth; and treat it until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer the spatule gently according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and to administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with fine tweezers and a suction tube, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water that enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing first with condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your thumb thin and light, and heat them a bit in the fire; and have the patient place one or pierce through his ear, and jump up from 1 foot to another part, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this of stone on stone until all the pus comes out completely, and thus it will come out entirely; and if you want, take some reeds, and put one end in the ear, and light the other end until the softer part of the reed is burned; then repeat with other reeds until all the pus comes out as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is small in body, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large in body that one can feel, then use the extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of ear worms when you cure it as we have said in the section and in the treatment of distillations, and if the cure does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if any worms appear, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the reed of which is the shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finest end in the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully on the entire reed; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, stuff around the reed with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven for worm removal, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which is the shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or of bronze it should be narrow below with small holes, and above open for distillation; and to press within the distillation a well-made bronze instrument for this purpose, and if you want use the dropper and wrap around the tip properly with cotton; then pour your oil or your juice, and what you wish from your medicines into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear; then put inside the dropper all the cotton, and press your hand moderately so that the oil is distilled into the earwax of the ear; and the patient feels it within, and the distillation should be slightly heated by fire beforehand as one distills it into the ear; and beware that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stuffing of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to the stuffing of wounds, or of flesh grown within the ear, and these stuffings sometimes come perfectly into the ear so that one cannot see it; and at times there is a little swelling blocking the hole, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes perfectly in and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many conditions, and for the one that can be seen, you must place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, then remove it completely with this spatula of such form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind completely so that it does not injure the ear; if the obstruction is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstructions are deep in the ear, then take a fine light scraper and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels difficulty in hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is sealed, or take a bandage and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must bleed the bandage and apply another soaked bandage made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papermakers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	These eyelashes that come from papermakers' eyes when they are moist and then dry, you must stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and cut them from the root with a spatula; then apply powdered vitriol to the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not fall out, then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is not moved much; and often they heal because something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come in the eyes things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of moisture thickened above and below the eye; the treatment is such: take notice if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is easy to know; then cut it widely, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit the parchment, do not worry about the patient; and if the split is large, sew it together with a stitch, and care for it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing forcefully, for the ointments will restore it quickly and encourage flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the wax is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the parchment, extend the wax with tweezers, and cut and press it from both sides; and if the parchment is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the wax is cut, wash the area with salt water, and treat the spot with something that encourages flesh growth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat which forms web-like threads on the eyelids, and this happens more to children than to any other people, and greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for that reason they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep thus, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist with exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exinach be gathered in the center of the circle; then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit as wide, but not larger than the wound you make in vein surgery; and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases exinach comes out from the slit, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then with one piece of cloth tightly held between your fingers towards the flame, and turn your hand right and left until it is scattered; and be careful not to put anything in the slit, that you do not reach all the way to the eyeball, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the abscess does not open at the beginning of the slit, then slightly enlarge the slit until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind ashes and put them on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then treat it with plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs other than those natural grow in the eyelids and are irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and opacities, to the point that it can lead to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: by cautery with fire, or by medicine as stated before in the chapter on cautery, and also done by incision and suturing or by cautery, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the eyelid to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, stick a needle through all the thread above; and do this near the edge of the eyelid where the hair grows next to these hairs, and pull the thread up over all the eyelid, and turn it with the razor; then cut in the part below the eyelid, below the attached hairs, along all the spatium from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove the thread, and place under the eyelid a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sew on top of the eyelid an interlaced figure like the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity by which you wish to lift the eyelid that is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And so there is such that requires one to cut a great quantity of the parchment according to how the parchment is softened; then slit all the spatula over the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tarsus up to the small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the circle, then peel it entirely; then join the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all one thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make dry the excess threads on the two eyelids with some sticky things, if you wish to do so; and if not, then have no concern, then leave the stitch and the threads up to three days or four; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and binding things, for the parchment rises at the closing of the wound and the joining of it, but the stitching is weaker (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: which is that you mark the parchment with a shape that is as like the leaf of myrtle, as we have related, three needles apart according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with thread, and pierce it through the area; and place one thread near the large eyelid, and the second thread near the small, and bring together between your fingers the threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have recounted, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the membrane are inverted: you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one case and the other is more intricate.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the eyelashes is according to this form: and it is that you turn the parchment and cut inside as I have said, and then make two eyelashes by art, and two subtle threads as long as the parchment and as wide as the spatula; and cut at the two ends where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly on what rises above the eye's parchment, and pull the two lashes from both sides properly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is constrained will die, dry up, and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with force, and treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sealed, and the parchment is lifted, the hairs will not grow back; and this is the form of the two lashes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put silk thread through it, thin and fine; then bring together the eyes and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the container another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then place the patient's head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is clear, for this is a subtle and delicate task, then put the needle all the way into the hair root at the site, and make it pierce the paper quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the container, and place in the container that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out of the container onto the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the shaft is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will draw the shaft from below to all the thread that you have ordered there, until the shaft comes out of the upper opening and you see it by the sight of the eye; then you will pull the shaft and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair burns in its place and flesh grows over; and if the hair is small, then accompany one long hair from natural hairs, and lift it with that which you leave, until it is extended and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways it occurs: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by the suddenness of a wound, or by cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work is that you split that union, separate its lips, and place linen threads inside, and leave it until it is healed; and it does not suit to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and the broth of water or ale and flaxseed should be cooked, and ointments of aquilon melted in any of the oils, and wrap a thread around it, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not mend according to the form it was before; and this work which we have said is no more than adjustments for this disease, so that it does not return in the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working with it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out two fingers away from the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the papery returns according to what it should, that is good; if not, then take the rasp and put it in the crack, and turn the papery, and cut two cuts on the side inside the papery; and let the heads of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called «I griesche»; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are sharp underneath from what surrounds the papery, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a woolen thread; then cure it with what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crack or a suture or a cautery, then you must cut a straight incision under the hairs of the papery, and according to what is said above; then separate between the two edges of a bandage, as I have said; and one must work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters devise ingeniously with all their might how they can return the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in working and using instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this union happens to men in such a way that the paper above is soldered with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural works, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you cut off what is adhering to the fine spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear if the sharp spatula wounds the eye; and your incision, with which you peel off that assembly, must be lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of that assembly is healed, and they sometimes use salty water in the eye, and raise it with sweet water, and collyrium; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool moistened with egg white; and after the third day use the collyrium and things soldering until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white moisture frozen, so when one touches it with iron and thinks to burn it off with tweezers, one cannot; and both appearances begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you operate the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then cut the nail with tweezers of small padding, and stretch it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair or ox hair or cattle hair, and strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the nail with thread and stretch it above, and scrape all the hair from the side of the nail that faces the pupil and sew to the hair up to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct all the way to the fine spatula and with small force, and leave the natural flesh or tear duct so that by the incision the usual course of tears does not come; and sometimes stretch the nail only to an inch, and with thread as we have said; then scrape it all with the above form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the flesh membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a bit of crushed gall, and from the collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then clean it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not firm, and you cannot push the needle in, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail-like condition is often treated with medicines; and they grow back as I have described in the section, and if you see it needs to be cut, then work on the patient’s eye, and take a slightly sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail gently from above, and if you see that it does not thin out and the flesh presses in, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and crushed gall, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the work again according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary to the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct is harmful to the eye by great damage, then suspend it with a lancet, and cut off part of it but not all, so that tears do not come; then drip into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the cornea
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the cornea, pressing on the eyelids and turning them outward, resembling a pomegranate rose; and the work is such that the patient places his head in your hand, then you operate on the eyes, cutting all that flesh with appropriate lancets for this purpose, holding it firmly; then cut the first layer of flesh, going straight to the scraper until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spatula we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and the small forceps with which you remove the sebaceous material, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of crushed saffron to which you drip red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place a cotton pad on the eye turned outward secured with egg white so that it does not cause a hot abscess; and if anything remains and the warm pus rises, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the hot abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh is attached in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb can withstand that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Swelled veins red that are covered over the eye, and they hinder the sight's work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then necessary first that you examine if the eye in which the swelling is, is protruding, and there is no other disease besides the swelling; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then suspend those veins for a whole anointing according to his wisdom, and let the anointments be doubly subtle according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then bind those veins subtly with force, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move out of the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the probes, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut beyond those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains of the bile.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot gather all of this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method that is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the binding:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician also calls a fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a method to cut into the abscess where it needs to be, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then scrape it all with this instrument here whose form is given; it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made of iron to the end that it reaches, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is scraped off; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the sinus is sealed and flesh grows there, and the core of the ulcer is sealed and remains this way for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other method than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the sinus according to this form: and that is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron and with strong medicines, and when it is uncovered take a probe according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and the shaft should be narrowed to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the lacrimal duct, and keep your hand a little away from the eye, then turn the probe entirely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the wind that comes out if he holds his hand over his sinus; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and the sinus hardens, the matter goes to the sinus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open in every part, and there comes no obstruction to the nerve, nor diminishment, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then place leeches or a cupping without striking to suck, then apply over the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloes and incense and storax, and then strain the eye, and plaster over with strips and cloths; and the method of the cloths is that you take cloths quite soft, and double each in four, and then place one over another according to the amount the eye requires; then strap above with a hard bandage firmly, and restart the leeches to suck without striking; then remove the leeches and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the bandage becomes softened, you must strain it very tightly; then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye improving, it is good; if not, restart the plastering and cloths and the bandage and leeches until it be healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of the woven skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the woven skin, then it opens up, and a kind of paper fibers come out like resin grains, which is astonishing to see; then if you see it cut, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the part underneath up to the upper part, then put another needle where there is double thread from the part of the eyelid; and have it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the skin around, and bind it well, then pull out the needle and put on the eye moistened wool in an egg white; and leave it until the threads fall with the skin, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is bound by the skin on both sides by a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great opacity, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes to a point at the edge of the eye, and drain the white moisture and lower the eye, and enter thus quickly; then extract until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than the white of the eye gathered together, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take his head between your two hands, and move it until you see the white come up to your eyes; then fix it so that it does not descend and disperse the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the white is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	seat the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut into the corneal membrane bit by bit along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the corona until the pus comes out; and when it is out, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then clean it further as needed until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; act according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and bind and tightly hold the healthy eye; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a hair at that swelling of the eye at the part of the lesser lachrymator, then forcefully insert the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand until it pierces into the swelling of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and the length of the path of almagda should be exactly equal to the distance from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, then put the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then squeeze it under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows out now, the patient sees it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a while, if the water rises through the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, then extract almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little; and then put back some sea gem water, and lift that eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye cotton or wool soaked in rose oil and hen's egg white, and bind with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin with hen's egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in the almagda, as we have said; and upon completing the work prepare for the patient a gentle sleeping posture, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition until the third day; then release him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put the binding back on until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate for you to do this during the time of treatment or after the incision now, but it must be lightened so that the liquid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If hot abscesses come, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and apply what soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed, then release the sight and put on his face an orilliet to cover for some days, and be thus in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the house little by little, and return to his usual habits; and know that no apprentice should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Yemen, who told us that in his country they make a device pierced with holes through which water is sucked, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new invention.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, for those who do not understand them see; and they are properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of the axes of this same fineness, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh is born on the nose with various attachments, of which some resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are such cases where the flesh is embedded in a fox-colored tone, and there is also smooth flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case then, of this smooth flesh which is not embedded, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work on his nostrils, and apply the uncinus to that flesh, and pull it hard; then cut what you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula from one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cut off, then open it all with fine and light instruments so that nothing remains; and if the blood overcomes you, or an abscess is hot, then treat it as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood is stilled and all the pus is removed, then apply a clean and moist dressing with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the dressing works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healing; and if moisture does not come through properly, know that there is dead flesh in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it is necessary that you put a slightly thick linen thread there, and tie it tightly with knots, and have between each knot space of one inch or less; and make the patient put the end of the thread into his nose as much as possible, and pull on the odorant until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children at school do this, and it is a simple thing for those who want to do it; then hold one end that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and pull off each knot in sequence as they are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the worms have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back to the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then place a plug of linen in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the method of the instrument to purge the head, into which one drips oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and guide it thus; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the tip of the nose, and it grows and becomes large quickly, such that it is quite noticeable to look at; and for this reason you should cut it off at the beginning, remove all of it, then apply the cautery or burning medicine to the area; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a dusky color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess, because when it is cut sometimes great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is slightly sensitive, not of a dusky color, and you see that it can be completely cut off, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
