And if you find rotten flesh in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut all the rotten part off and throw it away, then clean the wound; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound from which blood flows without stopping by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put in this powder which closes as soon as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; vitriol three parts, and powder them finely, and apply to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it dries well and adheres to all its blood; and then clean it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with vitriol alone, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in this state, one does not put this powder on it at all; but instead applies some digesting ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it gives off pus; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with a wound, and it is small, then I will extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other method but to leave the treatment and not apply anything binding, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and chicory also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce it at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut and blood flows out, open it, tie it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the thorn of the throat is cut or the channel, and the passage for food is preserved, sew the channel onto the neck bone, do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural form; then bind it properly, leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, remove it; and if there are bone fragments, extract all that you can, and those you cannot have, leave them until the wound becomes pus-filled, and clear and relieve the discharge; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if air escapes when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep and fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in at the first hour, nor bind it because the blood does not clot perfectly, and returns to the heart, killing the patient; but apply a drawing ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; there will be no spasm, nor trembling of heart nor strangulation from breathing; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with poultices and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and persists, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front, side, or back, treat it according to what is in front; if it is large, by suturing; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone and has cut pieces off, clean the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound fester so that the extraction will be lighter; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines fall out, causing internal intrusion; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound can be worse than a larger one because one does not immediately put the intestines back in; for when the intestines feel the cold they swell quickly, making it harder to put them back, thus the moderately sized wounds are better as one repeatedly places the intestines back in their place more easily. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: two common sutures occur in the suturing of the belly, and the other wounds of the body have two other specific sutures; yet they are still more specific to the suturing of the belly, and I will speak of each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestines comes out, and it is difficult to put back, this is due to one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in the following manner: soak a sponge or soft cloth in moderately hot water, or you boil in water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and wet the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this makes the wine restraining, and it is better to use alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling diminish, moisten the intestine with water in which aloes and mallows have been boiled, for by this means the entrance is eased; and if it cannot enter, cut a bit of the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than the incision, which should not be made without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: cut inward into the curvature and not outward, and see here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for that makes a difference.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, place your attention so that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds apply what is prepared for you, then take in your hands one pitiful minister who should fully cover the rupture with his hand and bring together the edges; this is the common method of sutures, which consists of taking a needle or more needles according to the size of the wound width, then leave two fingers’ space from the top of the wound and put in a needle with strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with the two ends of the saphenous vein, which is under the skin inside, until you make it penetrate that part, and bring together the two heads of the saphenous vein all four together; then tighten a double thread around the needle from both parts, then bring together the two sides of the wound properly, and leave another two fingers’ space, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to your need for needles until the whole wound is tied up; and the needles should be medium size, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be of medium size; and it is not right to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and harm the wound before healing; then cut off the tips of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths over the needle points to keep them tight, and leave them until the wound is healed; this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one needle or two The second common suture method is to bring together both sides of the skin and the two ends of the saphenous vein all four together with a single needle that has strong medium thread; when you have pierced these ends all four together, then continue sewing in the way clothes are sewn; leave a space between each stitch as wide as one minor finger; this stitching method is known by people, and I sewed a wound on a man’s belly which was cut by a knife, it was more than a palm wide, and two palms of intestines came out, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured up to 15 days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and push it from the outer side to the inner; when it has pierced straight through the center, then leave the head of the surface where you have pushed the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part to the outer; the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the leatherworker does with skins, and that you leave once the surface on one side, and take it back from the other, until the stitching is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galien properly described, is as some do, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the skin to the other end in such a way: insert a needle at the head of the membrane nearest, and pierce that place only, leaving the two ends of the skin; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part up to the inner part, at the two ends of the skin; then pierce one and the other from the outer part up to the inner part, at two other points on the membrane which are on the opposite side; and this is the most effective method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galien says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and one must insert one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew leather straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more severe than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgement of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, although the fire has moved it, then reset the intestine, and the cut; then put on the healing powder, and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present until the wound drinks; and stitch the thread, and let the sifac and the mirach be soldered; then treat the wound like others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on old cotton as soon as it begins to give drink, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many conditions when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you must moisten light wool in tempered hot oil or in rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in boils, which often happens, then cleanse them with warm black wine, and similarly if the putrefaction comes up to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the delicacy of the entire body, and its proximity in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the hernia jumps out of the wound, reset it just like the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must tie the place that is black so that no further bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the tie, and let the two ends hang from the part below the wound up to above to lighten the extraction when the hernia falls out, and the wound sucks in.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and excretions and gases came out of it; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to refine until he was healed, and the opening was sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sealed, I feared that the patient might have problems in his belly; and there was no problem, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a manner: take pins with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it over both edges so that it clamps its mouth down; and then cut off the head, and this stays so that it cannot untie itself, then put another pin after in the same way as before, until the entire wound is covered; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	They burn the head in the intestine, and it causes no harm to the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal’s intestine, in this manner: take the head of this intestine thread which should be very stripped down, and then tie to the head of this intestine thread the fine linen thread twisted together, then put the thread in the needle, and stitch the intestine, and sew it at the tear; and this method of sewing with guts is not far from according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is neither device nor health except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	about the fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it awakens, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is hairy and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth, a faulty nodulation, hard and white, where there is no pain, and it is also hairy like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times much; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or body; or by its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is porous, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption resembles pestilence; or by the property that the region has slow digestion and delayed healing, and is swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now you must know the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the spleen, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and there is such that comes to the main property of the member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you trust in its treatment, and you wish to know it, then take a needle of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, probe it with a fine needle of lead, for lead bends around the twists; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with needles, cleanse it through one of the openings, for moisture travels from one opening to another and cleanses it; then wisely probe as much as you can so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and this should be done carefully, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, cut it according to what I have said, and remove the infection and corrupted flesh that are inside; then treat it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply seated straight on, you should cut completely as much as you can, then put moistened needles with medicinal astringents in, push them to the head of the fistula so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; then apply healing ointments until it heals; and if it does not heal by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all the corruption is removed, then treat with healing substances until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and continues to leak as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: so uncover and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it heals thus, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other method but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with tongs, then pull it out with the appropriate tool for this purpose, and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving not one behind; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut away both moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound something that induces putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be removed more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then cleanse only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted area reaching to the marrow of the bone, you must scrape and cut right down to the corruption, and then treat it until it heals; and I will tell you of an ulcer that occurred in a man’s leg so that you may take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came within the body, until the matter reached the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no apparent cause for opening; but the physicians, by their folly, worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and a great deal of matter corroded out, and became an ulcer, and many openings developed where all kinds of pus and body moisture flowed out; and many doctors treated him for about two years, and there was no wise person in the art of hands until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what corroded through the openings with great force; and the body of the young man turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came opposite another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered part of the bone, which I found rotten and perforated; the corruption extended to the inner bone. I scraped away what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and began to treat the wound with poultices for a long time, but it could not heal. And then I started again, uncovering the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, scraped it away, and then removed it, and tried to close the area; but I had to cut around nearly an inch of the bone, and traced it out from all its parts, then treated it with medicines; and it healed quickly and closed up rapidly. And there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the bloodletting he would often bleed, but he was completely cured, and hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and it was well positioned and had no harmful or adverse effect whatsoever, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated this way: take a thread, and tie it at the end of the exposed bone, and command someone to pull it upwards; and place another larger thread made of wool on the flesh that is above the bone, and extend the head so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh in the place where you wish to sew, so that the needle does not injure the flesh; and put a coal or a piece of wood under the bone to move and cut the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to continue sewing as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and sew again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put the fire below, and then sew from one side to the other the corruption, and let the seam be as long as the corruption piece, just as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and sew the bone or where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, this thing is very difficult, but nonetheless you must examine that corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve get in your way; and know that the knives and the threads for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason you must prepare for each type of work its tool; and know that the work will show you the tool which you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases; so consider the tool which you need according to what it requires.
dou feu	of the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder rots either by an internal cause or by external force; and when you have treated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or from the evil, which is greater, of the lack of the limb; and the sign is that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, that corruption goes from member to member, and takes over the whole body; so hasten to amputate, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and basilisk and similar ones, if the corruption is at the tip of the toe, then cut it off, and do not give it time to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, cut at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his strength; and do likewise when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the next joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut all the foot off; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way except to leave the patient to death; and the method of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie above and below, and one minister holds one tie down, and another minister holds the other tie up, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ties a spatumile wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then cut or saw it off, and put on each side a cloth of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and cause the patient to have another injury and warm abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then quickly cauterize the place or put on some binding powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed like fire burning, and this corrosion first came on his toe of the foot, until it would spread over all the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed; and after some time the corruption returned at the finger of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on things that repel it after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corruptions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to because I had hope in driving back the matter; and also feared that if I were to cut his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak; and he completely despaired and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have this story only so that it may be done otherwise if there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in the fatty tissue, and stays for so long that it makes a large collection of pus; then it rots and bursts, and the pus jumps out, and leaves the place empty like some vessels; and the skin above is as thin as delicate cloths, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called «sain», and is not called «fistula»; but if it extends so far that it reaches to the bone perfectly, then it is called «fistula»; and you must cut all around this skin, especially when it is thin, like some cloths; and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear that the skin will heal and the corruption is not perfect, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it as follows: look to see if the swelling is large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then administer an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take assafoetida, oil, and white vitriol, equally, and cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey; then take according to your need from this mixture, and mix it with water and honey, and administer an enema to the swelling, and close the opening; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times, until the swelling is cleansed and the filth removed; sometimes it is treated with ash-water when this medicine is not present, which means taking ashes of vine wood, and pouring water over them, then filtering it, and administering an enema, until you know that the swelling is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ash-water, then administer an enema with water and honey in which there is a bit of powdered white vitriol mixed; or you may administer an enema of honey and wine mixed, for honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the swelling heal; and when you have done this, and you are confident that the swelling is well cleansed, then administer an enema with what causes flesh to grow in it, which means taking diaphoretic plaster, and mixing it with rose oil and wine; or you may administer an enema of certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatise on ointments; and if the opening of the swelling is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it slightly with a tool, and place some of the Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up leaving only one spot where the enema can enter, and if the opening that expels pus is at the top, cut it lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the wound is ripe, it does not let new flesh grow; and if you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, arrange in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place, for when the wound is ripe, it does not let new flesh grow and if you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, arrange in such a manner: that the pus runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the pus; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stretch over the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut forcefully at the opening of the breast somewhat wider than the first, then spread an ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to lighten the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after many days; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the pus, and know what runs from the pus, if it is venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the opening of the wound, know that the breast heals already, and health approaches; then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested phlegm after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle pus flows after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people to whom the healing of flesh in their wounds is delayed, and for those who do the opposite; and if undigested phlegm flows from the breast after many days, know that the breast will not heal; and if the breast delays in drying up and remains moist, then apply moist substances with a drying virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the final remedy; take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle old wine equally on the substance; then mix it and use it; and the same does better when honey is thickened, when diaphoretic ointments are not present, or take balm and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue the cloth and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes administer aristolochia longa and roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour of vetches and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them, make a powder, put it over the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption has become perfect, and makes an impression on the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; treat it with fistula treatment, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger of the hand, or of the foot, or by chance it may arise in other digits; and when it becomes old, and one does not take care, then comes the hot abscess, and it corrodes and throws out pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may corrode all of it; and corrosion comes up to the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the joint of the digit becomes swollen, and its color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail with one stroke, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh inside and begins to prick it and wound it, then you must put the knife under the nail that pricks the flesh, and lift it up, and cut off that flesh carefully and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it away and remove it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see that it must be corrupted, cut it as mentioned before, then treat it until it heals; and if it is inflamed, swollen, and he feels great pain, you must first cleanse it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by slicing across on top, and make sure the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocation that occurs in the hands of some men by chance is entirely fleshy, and by chance there is one where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them occur at the root of the joint, or the origin is in some ways of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The one that occurs in any knot of the finger does not move, and the one that occurs at the joint of the finger may move; the size of the fleshy one is slight, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one that occurs at the root of the joint is difficult to treat: be careful with cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with a hernia at the rear knot, you must first cut away the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone to an appropriate thread, then cleanse it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joint that comes to the hands together comes by birth, or by wound healing, or by fire burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that joint so the hernias return to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or oiled rags soaked in rose oil, so they do not join together; or you put between two pieces of fine linen until the joints are properly sealed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joint comes to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut that joint as appropriate.
des vils	of the villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large and full of superfluous melancholic fluids, which come to many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer a purge of bile to him, and then heal him with basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut it and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein, and draw it all out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is according to this method: first soak the leg in very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin, then remove the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then elevate and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can endure; and then tie it off, and instruct him to eat food that causes black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of it is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put him in a bath, and wash his leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then cut right at the vein from the long to the head of the knee, or in the part below at the ankle; then work on the skin with an incision, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when one touches it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems like a white string; then put the needle underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then scratch it lightly with a lancet, then cut another place three times afterwards; then scrape the skin on the vein until it appears, then lift it with a needle as you have done, and paint it with another lancet like you did first; then cut another size, or more if needed, then lift it, and cut at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second size; then extract from size to size until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle with all its thread doubled underneath, and tie and pull it, and put underneath a needle, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and this causes harm to the patient; and when you have completely extracted it, put on the place of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it off; and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the face is curved, and it does not cut through, so that it does not sever the vein; and it is of thick curvature, for if it were delicate, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil war
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This war is engendered in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and it may happen to arise elsewhere besides the legs, and this occurs due to the putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms come within the body, bred between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then changes the color, and begins the vein to forcefully issue forth, as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg; every time new blood comes out, wrap it again around the cloth, and tie it; if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause abscesses and rot in that place, a bad disease; for which reason it must be treated bit by bit until the top, leaving nothing behind on the body; sometimes this vein can be five palms or ten when treated, and once a man came to me whose vein was ten palms long; and when you cut it, you make one hole or puncture, pierce through to the bottom so that everything comes out; empty out the matter inside and apply healing medicines for several days to prevent rotting, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein there are fewer red blood cells, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or in the foot itself, and a lot of pus comes out, from which the red blood cells jump; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "ox sickness," because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves all over the body going up and down, and one can feel it well as it travels from member to member, until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and comes out; and it is engendered by the putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, serpents, earthworms, and ascarides in the stomach; and there is fear of its malice, for when it moves through the body, and climbs to the head, and reaches the eye, it might enter and destroy the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.
