Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the buttock and the kidneys and the hip, because these limbs do not allow for piercing over them, and it is only done to draw blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the child is teething; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the buttock to reduce the size of the limb; and removes pain when there is an obstruction or stone, it may by its attractive power accidentally remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place; and so does it when one puts them on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind; and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water alone or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping applied with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle one small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be made of glass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and it should have in the middle a crossbar of glass or iron, to hold a lit wick, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for the cupping devices for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping device on the limb in this way: take a wick of wax or linen, and put it inside the cupping device through the bar that is inside the cupping device, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping device so it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, with your fingers on the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor can escape, and remove the cupping device; and apply the ointment as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping then which is administered in disease of pleurisy, there is no tube nor pore, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only thus; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Bleeding is not administered except in limbs where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in bare parts of the flesh, such as toes or nails, and other similar ones; and the quality of use is that when you find leeches that are in clear sweet water without corruption, you take them; and put them in sweet water for a day until they are friendly and have nothing in their bellies; and then let it be bled by vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is an area where cups can be placed, place a cup there because that helps greatly.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the area of ash, and then with water, very well, and then apply it; and if the area heals too far from the bloodletting site, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the bleeding stops; and if the bleeding is multiplied, then put ground vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it stops; or you put on the area half of peeled beans, and leave them until they burn at the spot, now it will stop; and if you need more, take other bloodletting sites.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bloodletting sites do not want to take, then rub the area with fresh blood, or you stick a needle until the blood flows out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they burn; and when you see them fall, then sprinkle a bit of ground aloes and seil, or ash, now they will fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish doctors ignore this chapter, who have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter from them; and for this reason, the science is foreign in our land, because I have never found one good one. And I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I studied so much that I have treated the subject, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or crushing comes to anyone, you must hurry to treat the patient from one part to another, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or fainting, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and eat cold things, that is to say cold broths, and meat of fowl and veal, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, nor spreading of matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to their first proper regimen which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with foods that cause great nourishment, where there is viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the bone repairs itself and heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and frail people cannot heal or mend well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but it does not matter, set on the broken bone strong tendons which bind and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and it does not complete all of its work, and for this reason, it must be nourished with heavy foods, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that require elevation, and others in sharpening, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small裂纹。 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner have his own skill, and his proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes into its place; and the bone fracture is known by the limb being twisted, and it is clear by deficiency, and sound at the pressing of the hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or splitting, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	And it is not right that you move it by hand, but put on medicines that come here after, and then now restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes upwards, and the two parts are separated, they must now be put exactly equally, so that warm abscesses do not come; and if warm abscesses come, then leave it for some days until the abscess is calmed; then make it equal by moving it as lightly and skillfully as you can, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those which have pieces; then restrain it as it must be done hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, then extend it into two parts, if it is hands or feet, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset all by every means the joints in their places as much as you can, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then raise it gently, and do not tighten too much, nor press as those who cause by their work a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set properly, then instruct the patient well that he does not move it, neither while waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, then it is not set properly, and it must be placed in such a position that it feels no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that no deformity comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs differ in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: they must be wrapped with soft and fine linen cloths; and those which are large, such as thighs and legs: they must be wrapped with a broad and hard bandage, for wide bands embrace the entire large limb and bind it equally on all sides, so that there is no gap; then tie around light splints, three or four turns according to the limb, and press your hand a bit all over the bandage, then go above the break and press less, so that the break moves slightly away from the break; then loosen the bandage little by little until you reach a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again around the broken area; then return to the part below the break and bind moderately, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then put between the bandages linen splints or cloths so that everything is even, then tie all over with a binding, and then put your well-made plasters on it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put something soothing and warming for the abscess that reduces the swelling, and leave it like this for some days; then place on your probes, and let them be half a large cane in length, carefully prepared, or of wood from which arrows are made, or of palm ribs, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the probe which one places on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others; and let it be as long as suits the size of the limb, whether small or large; then place the probes just as you did in the first bandage, then bind over with thread appropriately, just as in the first bandage on the break; tighter below, then less so; and the threads should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like those foolish workers who make their bandages from twisted hemp cord do, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than two fingers' space between each probe.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of arrows after they are embedded in their flesh, put under them flax tufts, or torn wool, so that it does not bruise.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will speak of the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract arrows from all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to put in arrows stronger than after five or seven days, or more according to your security from a hot abscess ensuing; and here you have the method of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that sticks to the mill walls, and knead it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in various conditions, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the torsion: take З abareis and ladani and enule and asefetide and gum arabic and mugat, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana V З.; alechil IX З.; and make powder, and mix them with egg white; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is useful for torsion: take mugat and mallow, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana IX З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bole X З., and grind well, and boil with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and it alleviates the pain occurring, and surgeons use this on bone fractures: take new wool, and mix it with pitch and cooked oil, and place it on the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses, and they properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chicory, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of beans, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making a stronger plaster than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of chicory, and flaxseed, pomegranate rind, sweet clover, and pigweed, and flowers of violets and chamomile, one part of each; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb for restoration anything other than an ointment made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between two neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should put on the broken limb for restoration dry things somewhat warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take goat's milk and human nails cut, or bird feathers, and mallows, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and lay it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a bit afterwards, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not loosen it for several days And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, hasten, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take light cloth, and sea sponge moistened, and soak in water, and clean the place until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it for a day, until you are sure of no hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then restart the subtle binding, and a bit of plaster, and do not compress so tightly as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is warm and red and painful and swelling have all been removed completely, and you need a plaster and bandage, then restart it as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the limb, do not untie it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the fracture heals, and the fitting of the flesh advances; then restrain it more than before, and increase its flesh as I have said before; and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; then moisten it with warm tepid water every time you untie it, and this should be every third day, and lighten the binding a bit; through this work the nourishment comes to the limb, and quickly corrects what those foolish doctors do by restraining the limb improperly: this is bad, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing better than leaving it alone and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the neck removes all the bone down to the surface which is under the bone, just as an ax does to wood; and therefore this kind of fracture is called "chopping.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wounds of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a split from the edge of a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the tissue that is beneath the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason, this fracture is called "capillary"; and the wound that is made either by striking with stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it causes a piece of the bone to go inside, and the place is twisted like how blacksmiths strike on the cauldrons; thus, the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as a child's head; and it occurs with all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like stars; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the incision on them, and the probing that has been done, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is revealed by the fact that when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s accidents, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stiffness, trembling, ague fever, eyes coming out forcefully and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any astounding accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, otherwise the tissue under the bone will be corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part as follows: and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in every way you can, and over the area of the wound more than you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or a warm abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the warm abscess is calmed, and be sure of any bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods: one method is that you cut a narrow strip ahead, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various numbers of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and let them be pointed, and made of Indian iron; and work lightly so as not to bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you must pierce around it, either by making cuts with trepans, but not so deep that they penetrate beyond the skull bone, and there should be a margin or circle at the tip to prevent it from passing through the bone; and you must have several of these so that each fits the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepans for all skulls; and this is the form of the three types of trepans:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place the drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the drill to another part a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand or with any of the tools that you have such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you remove the roughness that remains on the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be finer and more subtle than other incisors; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with the tools; then clean the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is what Galen says, which is more safe; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone where the fracture moves openly, so that when you have uncovered that part, then place under the head of this lens-shaped incisor, of which here is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is angled on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet, so that you gently chip around the entire bone, and be careful of the tissue underneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut on top, and there are small pieces, then you must address that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you should have various sizes, to apply in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then use large scrapers first, and then finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and fine fractures, you must adjust according to its alignment; and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the surface, then administer another layer above it without compressing too tightly until it stains the wound only; and leave it thus for one day or two until the abscess is cooled, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, meal of vetches, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and immediately apply non-irritating medicines; and ensure that the wound is kept clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow anything to congeal over it, because when something congeals over the cloth of the brain, it will corrupt and harm it, causing great mischief to the patient; for when one puts a corrosive substance on the surface, it will harden above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no blackening comes other than from the medicine that has been put on, which has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue one cloth, and lay it on the surface; then treat it in the manner of treatments that is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, nor does it cause to bend or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your little finger in the hole of the nose, and place that break inside with your index finger, and push gently until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the fingers cannot reach the place, then you must put it equal at the head of a rod a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation has calmed down, then put a wad of linen cloths at the end of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you place one part against another where the break is; and let the threads be so thick that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some say that one should moisten the threads with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened with egg white and flour powder; then leave the thread until the bone is hard and the cartilage has stiffened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose quills in the nose instead of threads, and wraps a cloth around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through them; do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the neck while you are working there, then apply a poultice or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in the juice of daisy.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster by force, of sesame flour and frankincense powder, cooked with egg white, then place light bandages on top, and do not tie the neck; and if the break in the neck is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew the wound, and treat with things that heal flesh, and cause to mend, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the neck, then treat it with threads, and put in splints until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured below, and there is no wound on the outside, and the break is only on the outside, and is not split into two, but rather folded inward, it is recognized as a slight one.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, then put your right hand’s index finger, and push the fracture inward slightly, and align it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is split into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from two parts, until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or rupture, then I extract them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw cerate, and put on the cloth double; and put on the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then accurately reset what has changed; and put a plaster on it, of mill powder with egg white or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put on the plaster light wool, and if the plasters dry out, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reset it if no piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the bone is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place equally the fracture in your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or of wool, and let it be large according to your necessity; and extend and lift the bone, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you place equally the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the clavicle out due to it being stuck, then it is necessary that the patient lies often on his back, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and the assistant pushes the shoulder down until the bone of the clavicle is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, then you must cut above; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then cut it with one of the incisors that you have; but place this instrument under the clavicle to protect the skin.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not closed, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and let it have two ends, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the tear in the wound you made when you pulled out the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, sew the wound, and if the tear is small or you fear a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and lard and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The compression of the bone, when there is no wound and no cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster made of mill powder and egg yolk, and place light bandages over it, and put a sphere under the sound board if you need it; then take a very large band one palm wide, then put a double cloth over the bandages and the plaster; then take a slender stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that band, so that the end of the band hangs down; and place the stick on the break, and turn the band around the neck, and under the sound board and under the diseased board; and repeat from each side, and when you see that the band holds the break well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the ligature loosens, then tighten it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small cushion under the board while he sleeps to lift the shoulder up; this will lighten the break by the lifting of the shoulder, or tie his arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, until twenty days; then restart the plaster if you see that it is needed, and compress and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is restored in no more than twenty-eight days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It seldom happens that the shoulder is broken at its broad part or in the middle, and one would only know it by touching; then set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways you can; then put on the place flour with egg white, and light bandages, and lay a double cloth over it; then put on a wide and thin board slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there is any unevenness under the board at some part of the shoulder, use linen hair to fill in so that the board lies evenly; then bind it tightly with a large strap so that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten it, and realign the board if it moves from its place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number of days is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that shifts lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points beneath the heart, cut above it, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the rib to soothe an abscess that is hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breast fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The breast is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the lower part.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it droops downward, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of breath, and immediately, and perhaps vomits blood, and the intestines appear in the broken bone, and it can be well seen.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs from both sides with your hands, and delicately adjust equally in all ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the thin stick of salt or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it firmly on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the binding around the back and tighten moderately, and renew the binding every hour, and if it loosens, then tighten it; and if it needs to be untied due to corruption or itching that comes at the site, or pain or abscess, do so promptly, untie it, remove the plaster, and address what has occurred with methods of treatment; then reapply the plaster and bind until healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs only occurs in their thick parts behind the back, and at the head inward, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel this well upon examination with the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you place the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is leaning inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as though from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and they have a sharp pulse, and immediately vomit much corrupted blood, and this is of severe sickness, and the ancients put great ingenuity into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, to push the windbreaker into the lower region.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not wish for hot abscesses to come there, if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come there, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we apply cupping to the area to bleed thoroughly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping may draw the excess to the area due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the heat around, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the site of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place under an instrument to guard the surface; and then one must cut the bone, pull lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then put on cloths moistened in rose oil, and place them on the site; and treat the area as is necessary for an abscess, and let the patient lie on their side where it should be, until healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break to the neck bones, and it often happens that it bends; and likewise with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened, swollen, and numb, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if the legs are weakened, and if the symptoms are present that occur in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary discharge; and when they are examined on their stomach, there is involuntary discharge.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to saddle up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: do not labor too much in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is a hot abscess, you apply thorn apple oil or egg white oil until it is calmed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where the pain is felt until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cut into the chest; remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, then treat with ointment until healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the collarbone," you place your left hand pouch there, and equalize it with the other hand to your ability, then apply the plaster and splint if needed; then bind it tightly, and if there are dislocated bones, cut into them, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight thinning at the top; and it makes the long side lean inward, and the patient feels pain at the site, and pricking, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it until you are on the fracture; and know what the fracture and its shape are; and if the fracture is only at the top, make that fracture equal so that it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is on the long side and it leans inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is aligned for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put on the poultice, then place a wooden or horn splint over it, and bind the bandage so that it does not move; and apply the site beneath the ribs until the length is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are calmed, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and bind it as appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a stick of medium thickness, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two ties, and pull them up, and seat the patient on a chair; then throw his broken arm over the stick until it reaches the armpit, and have a wooden support in the middle, then pull upwards on some weight or let the attendant stretch downward; then the doctor places the splint equally in both hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that the patient is placed on his back, and his hand is tied to his neck, then command two attendants, one to hold what is above the splint with both hands, and the other to hold below at all times, and each stretches their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction should be stronger, then hold the limb below the fracture and above the fracture, and stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, then you must place one bandage under the arm, and another toward the side, below the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is toward the side, then you should put the bandage lightly, without strain, until the fracture is even on its place, and on the side; then set the break evenly as it should be, and bind it, unless hot abscesses come.
