Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if hot abscesses come, then do not bind it until the seventh day, and put wool soaked in egg and rose oil on it until the hot abscesses are calmed; then bind it, and the method of binding is that you put a plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and bind it at the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm is in its natural position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you fear that the bone may move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one inch of space, and let each splint be so large that it extends three times beyond the break on each side; then strain on the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, more tightly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the straining as we have said, at the hour when you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it tied until the seventh day as we have said; then examine every three days the binding so that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is directed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, then do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion filled evenly with wool, and check every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor the ligaments soften; direct it by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be coarser.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be reset in forty days altogether; and then one must loosen them and administer baths and medicinal ointments to properly align the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and embedded, it remains to untie for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "forearm bones," of which one is small, and it is the one that leads to the wrist; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large forearm bone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small forearm bone is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small splint that is merely broken, then it must be slightly stretched gently, and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large splint, then it must be stretched more forcefully; and extend it on the cushion, and raise the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or to the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the doctor makes it even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each in its place, and if any detached piece pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the trephine to wound, I have spoken of it in a special chapter; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses occur hot, then glue a cloth with cerate made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth gently over it until the hot abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and put on a plaster of mill powder with egg white, then place the stars, and let the star of the trephine be stronger and somewhat wider than the others; and know that there must be six stars on the arm in various arrangements: whether the trephine is in one of the bones or two; and press more on the trephine than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are over the trephine be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must rinse the member with warm water, until the itches are calmed; and let the member rest not too tight.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the binding, and if the joint is softened and the bones separated and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be careful if the nourishments cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a bit, and leave it this way for some days until the nourishments flow in, and then bind it tightly.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And then he can place his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the joints of the fingers there are few breaks, and they do not come but with much bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit crosswise, and sit straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on the stretched cloth, and the attendant stretches the broken bones, and the doctors make them equal until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if no abscesses come, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the outside around the belly of the sole, then make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken sole; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the stick used for binding be as thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the back, then you must place a stick on top and another underneath on the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the joints of the fingers, if it is swollen, then set it straight as needed; and bind it with the sole, and if you wish, place a small straight stick to elevate the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, then set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger next to it; or you bind them all together while keeping them immobile, or place a stick on top as with the thumb; and be careful in the restoration and in the placement of hot abscesses, and support what comes up, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns front and back; and the restoration is such that one ties a bandage above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends his bandage on his side equally; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the bandages should be towards the hip, and the other bandage below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is near the knee, then the bandage should be close to the knee, and the extension downward; then the physician places the bone straight with both hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then applies the plaster, and binds it, provided abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it calm down before returning to your work and treatment; the task is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap on the fracture a thick bandage doubled in II or III, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and put I long thread between the thigh and the leg, below near the knee, and bring the head of the thread above; then wrap the bandage on the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then use the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the pressure even, then begin to tie firmly III or IV turns on the fracture; and as you go higher on the fracture, it is less constricted; then take hold of II ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie III splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread until you come near the foot; and bind so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, provided no abscess or swelling or other similar thing occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then he undoes it and arranges what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hurt, then they must be washed out, if one can; and if one cannot, then one must split the place and pull out forcibly; and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that one must insert splints, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 50 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the kneejoint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee joint there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no more than a crack, or a perforation, and this happens in open wounds and without open wounds, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put equal pressure on what is round at its ends until it is assembled as much as can be moved; then apply the plaster, and place a rounded splint if needed, and bind it appropriately; then treat all the conditions we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar ones; apply to each accident what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is properly named "tibia", and the other is called "femur"; and all types of fractures happen as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and make it equal, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that fit the leg on both sides and be as long as from the knee to below; then wrap in two layers one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle likewise, so at this point the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some apply one board as long as the leg, and if it is of wood, put the leg there to guard against movement, and properly do this in the break where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so treat until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle no break comes, but to the bones of the foot sometimes a break comes and to the toes a little, and there is force that shatters in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot are broken and you see these bones protrude over each other, then place such patient's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and bandages on top, and place under the sole of the foot a small board filled with two mixtures, then bind it to the approaching foot properly, after you have wrapped cloths around, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then loosen the binding, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any fingers broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a bit wider, then place under the foot that board I have mentioned, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it stand at the top of the board so as to protect the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and address each incident as appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the break of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the female's natural part is broken, have her sit extended, then incline her toward the back side, and hold her from behind; then fill the hand with cotton for the woman's natural part, and put in as much as a thumb; then make the woman stand up, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton jumps, until it comes to the entrance of the natural part, and the bone returns with the thumb; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or around: the break will be restored, and if you want, take a bladder of goatskin, tie a cane to the opening, and put all the bladder into the natural part; then blow into the cane strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside: the natural part will return the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it that way for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of the man is broken, or of the woman, restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these breakages are not hidden to one who puts his study and practice into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fractures indicate in various positions the right way of restoration: understand them then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or even longer, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that he be bled now, so that the bleedings we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then stop it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume restoring the break in the same hour, or on that day, unless hot abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses come, then delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscesses are calmed, and do not touch it on the third day nor the fourth, for you would cause a harmful accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered chest, then you must set it lightly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to set it evenly with your hands, then reset it with this instrument which is made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and therefore it is necessary for the physician to prepare three or four, according to what is needed for each treatment of the fracture; and let it be round and a bit thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called “palainche”, for which the head of the bone should be placed on top of the visible bone; and he pushes once, until it returns, and is equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is delicate, and the instruments cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the head of the bone so that the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, whether an incisor or saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small shards.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with black styptic wine, and clean if it is necessary; and do not put on the wound plaster or anything else that has oil, so that it does not cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not squeezed with the fracture; and many times foolish doctors have done this, and have caused death or sometimes corrosion on the patient; and let the squeezings be softer and more gentle than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that harmful accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not put salves on it; but wrap around, instead of salves, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound is growing around the incision, remove what you have put on top with pure wine, and apply a healing salve to the wounds, such as tetrafarmacón and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and whole.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that the wound heals downward gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but keeps opening, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another kind of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not touch it, for often death follows, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come upon the joint
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a disfiguring thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the knot is fresh: administer styptic medicines to it, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the knot in wads, and bind well, and do not untie for several days; then loosen it, and start another one, until the knots are removed; or apply it to a piece of plaster properly made; for the property of the plaster is that it removes all swelling above the limbs; and if the knot has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, cut on top of it, and slit the apparent excess; or shave it with some razor until it is removed, and treat until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and after remains the limb weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive applications; or from too great movements, not at their proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, thus is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat well and soften the body so that blood multiplies within him; and administer baths and give joy and rest; then apply pitch on the limb so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and frequently wash it with warm water until the nourishment flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the form of the limb is ugly, it still does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great harms come from it, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the knots and tortures are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or herbs with softening properties should be boiled, such as leaves of mallow, roots, and mallows, and similar things; and you make a softening plaster, just as Dyaquilon does well, and you take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or linseed oil, and apply a plaster over it; or you take fat figs, and grind them with colt's foot, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodule is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the limb be moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened and stiffened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it must be cut until the bone, with a subtle and gentle incision; and apply care and diligence in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then he must now bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, then the limb swells, and perchance it is reset with great pain in its place; for this reason, it does not befit to move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times it brings about spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, then have the patient bled, then leave it until the swellings are all calmed; then wash the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jaws are dislocated here, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are slightly displaced from their places and softened a bit; or they are entirely dislocated, hanging towards the worse side, and drools out of the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and fully dislocated, then you must reset it quickly, without delay; and in such a manner that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and the physician puts his thumb of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other fingers of the hand should be spread out, to make it even; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor places it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reduction is difficult, especially if it concerns both jaws together, then wash them with hot water and oil, until you reset them lightly; do not delay in resetting them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset equally and the patient’s mouth closes well without being softened, then put a cloth moistened in an unguent made of rose oil and wax on it, then lightly bind it with soft bindings; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his shoulders between two cushions so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor strain to chew, but eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jaws are set; and then let him eat what he wants lightly, without exerting himself to open his mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be perfectly reset within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fevers and customary sweats occur, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from the rib within its connection to the breast, and it is sometimes dislocated outward, and this is felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and extends his arms; then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bind it tightly; and the joint towards the side cannot dislocate; if not, and if it sometimes does dislocate, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the poultice and bind it tightly, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way the shoulder of the back is reset when it is dislodged from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is when it dislocates at the lower part towards the armpit; and the second is at the side part towards the back; and sometimes it dislocates upwards, though this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inward due to the nerves; and most often it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for with them it dislocates quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it may happen to some men that there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must then test it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocation is recognized when it moves downward toward the armpit, creating a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear distinction between them; and you will find a depression at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit upon touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a bird's egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck nor move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new or if the person is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up, then places the fingers under the shoulder blade, and lifts the joint upwards with force to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, extends it up, then puts it under; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the attendant moistens with soothing and relaxing ointments, such as decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and should be anointed; then the patient is made to lie on his back, and under the shoulder blade a piece of wool is placed, neither too soft nor too hard, then the doctor places his heel upon the wool, and raises the head of the shoulder forcefully, and pulls the patient's hand; and another attendant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; the shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to reset it in this manner: and it is that you make present one who is larger than the patient; and he stands sideways, and puts his shoulder under the patient’s shoulder blade, and lifts upward, so that the patient hangs from the bar; and another attendant pulls the patient's hand downward towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then something heavy can be with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also reset in another way: and that is to fix the long stake in the ground so that the shoulder is as tight as a pistal, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but let there be cloths over it, and the patient stands along the length of the stake; then extend his hand down on the other side properly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things we have said, do this treatment: take a stake two arms wide and four fingers thick, which has one end smooth enough to enter perfectly under the shoulder blade, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind above the head of the wooden stick with soft cloth so that the wood does not wound the patient, then place it under the arm of the patient; and stretch out his arm on the long stick, and bind the shoulder to the stick, and the arm at the wrist, then put the arm on a step of a wide ladder, and let the hand be extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, then you must put under the arm a sphere of equal wool, then apply a plaster mixed with mill powder, along with incense and egg white, on all of the shoulder and around it, then strain under the arm appropriately, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then eats more after five or seven days, and moves it; and if it is stiff and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is displaced due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then you must apply cauterization at three points, as it is set out in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the armpit, and the breasts, or behind, is done by impulse, and stretching of hands, and another place is administered; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing cracks appear in the limb, and delays in movement, then the patient should take baths many times until those cracks are alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated bit by bit, and returns bit by bit; and if it is dislocated entirely, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back, because one can see it well and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is locked, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before hot abscesses occur, for if hot abscesses were to come, then it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and possibly leading to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset, you extend his arm with both of your hands; and his arms should be spread out, and the hands of the healer around, above and below, pressing the joint at its edges together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and trust in the root of the palm the thumb which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and two ministers extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on both sides, after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth; and when the healer has joined the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then forcefully put the joint back, until it returns; and once it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg white, tightly bind it, suspend the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or put on the joint a piece of fat sheepskin, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the skin back on, and then enter the bath again; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you wish, put on cow dung moistened and heated with butter, and apply it firmly; thus it will return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the reduction is light, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it dislocates, lest the area swell or a hot abscess develop.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is such that you place the affected hand on a table, and the assistant stretches the hand, and the physician places their hand equally, so that they put their palm on the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns. Nevertheless, it must be that you check if it is properly in place; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table during the extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then place the patient’s back of his hand on the table, and the doctor places his hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. If not, then strain soothing plasters on the abscesses, and leave it thus without recurrences.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and does not harm the patient’s strength while the hand is weakened, and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is no other remedy than to cauterize near the site, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any soreness, bathe it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on all sides, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the front; then stretch the finger and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then hold the tip of the finger and pull towards the side where it is separated; leave it for two days, and then make it even that day; and at night bind it as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and bind it again at night; do this often until it becomes tight. And in the same way you do if it is dislocated on the front of the hand, and do as you did before until it is healed; and in the same way you do when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the vertebral column
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebral column of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the excretions come out without will, and cannot be held back, and often some limb is weakened, or both thighs or both arms or one. And often the vertebral column moves in four parts; the one that moves at the back is called "rickets": the cure is to reward if the rickets came from childhood: there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And for those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients spoke of methods of cure with great words, but they did not have much benefit at all; but I have abbreviated according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hunchback which comes to the chest first, there is no remedy nor health; and likewise that which comes straight across two sides, and one cannot cure except properly that which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in a level place, and have padding underneath him so he does not injure himself; then stick one pole at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the boards of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two poles; and be well secured, the poles as we have said, and the doctor put his palms on the hump firmly until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient be on their side, and put the head of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the physician put his feet on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with a wrench that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fix two pegs at the head of the patient's great arm and towards the feet two others, and there be between each peg, above and below, a palm’s space in length; and have in each peg one hole where the wrench turns, and let the pegs be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each two pegs have one turning peg on which the ropes turn, and have in two turning points two small pegs of a palm’s length to turn the wrench; and then tie the rope which is among the boards to the wrench towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other wrench, and each of the ministers turns his wrench to the whole rope, and the master sets the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, then put on a drying poultice with an abundance of egg, and then the wads, and then the stick from a tablet three inches long, which properly indicates the site of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing, one must administer softening and relaxing medicines, with the stick that we have mentioned above; and sometimes one administers a piece of linen, and sometimes the appearance comes to the rear spine of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; and it is the bone that protrudes, for which one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that in the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only dislocations occur, not as in other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than others, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its internal dislocation is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the sick knee opens more than the healthy one, and the sick cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the area next to it swells with a hot abscess because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one to whom it comes to fail, is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens in front is that they stretch their leg according to the fulfillment; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and the ankle swells, and when they go, they step on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens behind is that they cannot extend their knee nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip joint is in a position below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are that you reward if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, there is no treatment; and it does not require any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.
