And for those whose dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, you must hurry to return the joint, extend it inside and outside, and move it left and right; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare one assistant to strongly extend the leg with both hands, or by means of a rope tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand over it in such a way that he places his hands under the bones, then tightly binds with a single strong bandage on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and they all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four types, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to treat its type When the dislocation is inward, you must lay the patient on his healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the spot which is below the joint, then extend the bandage upwards towards the joint, and towards the spine; then let another assistant hold his arms, and grasp the thick part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it upwards strongly: thus it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner that we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be stretched out two times longer than the other; then let him hang from the head of a post, and be two arms' length off the ground; then command one assistant to grasp the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who holds the thigh firmly, for the joint now returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the thigh, the patient lies down, as we have said in that which has gilbositeit, and binds the limb on the sick leg properly, and on the foot also; then puts two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then sticks one torch between the thighs of the patient in the form; and has planted moist cloths around so it does not hurt the patient, then extends each minister towards him, and the doctor places equally with his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table, and press it as we have said in the case of gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and let the doctor put his hand on the sick joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the patient down or lift up on the ground, but it should be as if the hip were dislocated at the back, just as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should lie on his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table; and it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal; then align the thighs, and apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then unbind him, and put the plaster on again; and if you see them to be equal, then bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not touch the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another minister extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it touches his thigh slightly; and apply the plaster and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then unbind him; and the patient should not labor to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not fully extended, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and extends forward at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is light, and one should gently extend it by hand when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you must make the patient sit straight, and have one assistant firmly grasp the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly place a pole between his thighs, and wrap cloths around it so as not to injure the patient; then have one assistant grasp the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot by hand or with a bandage tied above the ankle; then each assistant should extend equally, and the pole should be between the patient’s thighs to hold him in place when he is being extended; then the doctor places his hands equally on the dislocation, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, then put the plaster and bandages on, and bind tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are above the heel behind, so that the binding is not too tight; then leave for two days or three, and if the binding softens, then tighten it again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then you must soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, then they must be gently extended without strain, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table straight, and put your foot on what appears of his joints, then press with your foot strongly until it returns; and when it is even, and nothing appears, then put under the sole of the foot a board at two ends, then pull strongly, and leave for three days, then loosen it; and have it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation and one wants to restore it, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and cautious, not bold; and use at the beginning things that calm a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the limb to its place, although a hot abscess may come; and when the limb is in place, administer things that calm a hot abscess, and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are loose, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear according to what I have said, for it does you no good according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arm and your body.
Amen	Amen
